**Rule:** Remove unused code paths (e.g., HTTP method mappings, enum cases) rather than keeping them for hypothetical future use; they can always be added back when actually needed.

### 20. Wrap Handlers In Usecallback

**Source PRs:** #40404, #42125, #40461, #43863, #44843, #42476, #42128, #42071, #42763
**Modules:** frontend

---

### 21. Batch Database Lookups Instead Of Per Item Queries
**Rule:** When checking or retrieving data for multiple items, use a single batch query (e.g., `findByIds`) and filter the results in memory, rather than making a separate database call for each item.

**Category:** performance
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 1.0
**Review count:** 13
**Source PRs:** #45147, #44991, #40900, #42583, #47156, #42521, #44515, #46827, #47189, #46171
**Modules:** guardrails, environments, projects, extensions, workspace-all, frontend, registered-models, apps
**Trigger:** You're writing code that needs to check or retrieve data for a collection of items, and you're about to place a database or API call inside a loop or map operation that iterates over each item individually.
**Rationale:** Issuing a separate database query per item creates an N+1 problem that scales linearly with collection size, causing latency spikes and unnecessary database load. A single batch query reduces N round-trips to 1, dramatically improving response times and reducing connection pressure on the database.

---

### 22. Extract Complex Expressions Into Named Variables
**Rule:** Extract complex string interpolations or expressions into separate named variables to improve readability, especially when a similar pattern is already used nearby.

**Category:** code-organization
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 1.0
**Review count:** 13
**Source PRs:** #46468, #41287, #47142, #40827, #45418, #43983, #45471
**Modules:** projects, dataset-rw, extensions, frontend, apps

---

### 23. Handle Absent Entities
**Rule:** When code looks up an entity that may not exist (deleted, archived, never created), handle the absence explicitly — clean up stale references, provide fallback behavior, or defend against null returns.

**Category:** error-handling
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 1.0
**Review count:** 13
**Source PRs:** #47170, #47189, #47216, #40765, #42403, #46352
**Modules:** server, apps, model-serving, nucleus
**Trigger:** You're writing code that looks up an entity by ID or reference — such as a project, dataset, model, or user — where that entity could have been deleted, archived, or never created.
**Rationale:** In a long-lived system, entities get deleted, archived, or orphaned constantly — code that assumes a referenced entity always exists produces 500 errors, broken UI states, and stale data that accumulates silently. Handling absence explicitly keeps the system self-healing and gives users clear feedback instead of cryptic failures.

---

### 24. Method Names Should Describe Behavior
**Rule:** Method names should clearly communicate their behavior (e.g., include 'latest' if the method returns only the most recent result) so callers understand semantics without reading the implementation.

### 25. No Self Referential Package Imports

### 38. Include All Available Context In Audit Events

### 39. No Classname With Styled Components
**Rule:** When using styled-components, do not use `className` for styling — use styled-component composition instead. Reserve `className` as a last resort for deeply nested third-party components you cannot reach otherwise.

**Category:** code-organization
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 1.0
**Review count:** 10
**Source PRs:** #41123, #41121, #44912, #44526, #44615, #41818, #41746
**Modules:** frontend
**Trigger:** You're styling a React component that uses styled-components and you're tempted to add a className prop or CSS class to apply styles.
**Rationale:** Mixing className-based styling with styled-components fragments the styling model, making it harder to trace where styles originate and breaking the single-responsibility principle that styled-components enforce. Keeping all styles in composed styled-components ensures colocated, predictable, and refactorable style definitions.

---

### 40. Prefer Unknown Over Any For Passthrough Types
**Rule:** Use `unknown` instead of `any` when a value is simply passed through without being accessed — it provides type safety while still allowing forwarding.

### 41. Push Pagination To Database

### 44. Avoid Unnecessary Option Wrapping

### 45. Avoid Nested Ternary Expressions

### 46. Avoid Unsafe Option.Get In Scala
**Rule:** Eliminate unnecessary Some() wrappers that force downstream .get calls on Options; restructure code so the Option is handled cleanly without calling .get, which can throw at runtime.

**Category:** error-handling
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.9
**Review count:** 9

**Modules:** server, model-serving, apps

---

### 47. Catch Nonfatal Exceptions Instead Of Runtimeexception
**Rule:** In Scala, catch NonFatal(ex) instead of RuntimeException to avoid swallowing fatal errors like OutOfMemoryError while still handling all recoverable failures.

**Category:** error-handling
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.9
**Review count:** 9
**Source PRs:** #40643, #40765, #46682
**Modules:** nucleus, model-serving, gen-ai

---

### 48. Consistent Domain Terminology In Naming
**Rule:** When the codebase uses synonyms (e.g., 'run' and 'execution'), keep naming consistent within a bounded context; if a DTO uses 'Run', the corresponding domain class should too, unless the name is scoped to a different local context.

**Category:** naming
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.9
**Review count:** 9
**Source PRs:** #45390, #43815, #46051, #40989, #45003, #41115, #47131
**Modules:** server, projects, gates, frontend, activity, dataset-rw

---

### 49. Derive State From Props Instead Of Useeffect Plus Usestate
**Rule:** When a value can be computed from existing props or state, calculate it directly (or use useMemo) rather than syncing it through a useEffect into a separate useState, which adds unnecessary complexity and re-renders.

**Category:** performance
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.9
**Review count:** 9
**Source PRs:** #42003, #42049, #41992, #41878, #42848, #45910
**Modules:** frontend
**Trigger:** You're adding a useEffect that watches props or state just to update another piece of state with a computed or transformed value.
**Rationale:** Every useEffect + setState pair introduces an extra render cycle — React renders once with stale state, then immediately re-renders with the updated value, causing unnecessary work, potential UI flicker, and harder-to-trace bugs when dependencies drift out of sync.

---

### 50. Include Context In Debug Log Messages
**Rule:** Debug log messages should include sufficient context (e.g., the object being operated on) so that logs are useful for troubleshooting without additional instrumentation.

**Category:** logging
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.9
**Review count:** 9
**Source PRs:** #41291, #40549, #41010, #41007
**Modules:** e2e-tests, model-serving, domino-cost

---

### 51. Include Domain Context In Error Messages
**Rule:** Error messages should include domain-specific context (e.g., entity type, identifier) so that engineers debugging production issues can quickly identify which resource and operation failed.

**Category:** error-handling
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.9
**Review count:** 9
**Source PRs:** #45957, #41287, #46129, #40052, #42511, #43792, #40643

### 52. Inline Single Use Transformations
**Rule:** When transformation logic is only used in one place, prefer keeping it inline rather than extracting it into a separate method, to reduce indirection and keep the code easier to follow.

### 56. Reuse Existing Constants Over Creating New Ones
**Rule:** Before creating a new constant, check if an existing one already serves the purpose; if a default constant's value is insufficient, increase it rather than introducing a confusingly-named duplicate.

**Category:** code-organization
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.9
**Review count:** 9
**Source PRs:** #40873, #42755, #44102, #45379, #46751, #46901, #43122

---

### 57. Shared Mutable State Requires Explicit Thread Safety Controls
**Rule:** When state can be accessed by multiple threads, add explicit synchronization — protect both reads and writes using a dedicated lock object or volatile + synchronized pattern.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.9
**Review count:** 9
**Source PRs:** #41307, #40505, #42260, #43112
**Modules:** service-health, executor, common, server
**Trigger:** You're introducing or modifying mutable state (vars, mutable collections, caches) in a class that can be accessed from multiple threads — such as service health checkers, executor managers, or shared singletons.
**Rationale:** Unsynchronized shared mutable state causes silent data corruption, lost updates, and stale reads that surface as intermittent production bugs — especially under load when thread interleavings become unpredictable. Explicit locking with a dedicated lock object makes the concurrency contract visible and auditable.

---

### 58. Test Description Must Match Assertions
**Rule:** Ensure that the test description accurately reflects what the test actually validates; if it claims to test a behavior change, the test must trigger that change and assert the result.

**Category:** testing

**Review count:** 9

### 66. Verify Mock Interactions In Tests
**Rule:** When wiring mocks in tests, add verification that the mocked methods are actually called with expected arguments — otherwise the mock only prevents crashes without validating behavior.

**Category:** testing
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.9
**Review count:** 9
**Source PRs:** #47177, #40643, #46809, #46978, #45086, #46468
**Modules:** workspace-all, model-serving, ppm, dataset-rw, server, projects
**Trigger:** You're writing a test that wires up mocks or stubs for dependencies. You need to ensure the system under test actually invokes those dependencies with the correct arguments, not just that the test passes without exceptions.
**Rationale:** A mock that is wired but never verified only prevents NullPointerExceptions — it does not confirm the system under test actually performs the expected collaboration. Without interaction verification, production code can silently skip critical operations (database writes, event publishing, API calls) and tests will still pass green.

---

### 67. Aria Labels Human Readable

### 68. Avoid Ts Ignore Unless Truly Necessary

### 69. Avoid Usememo For Trivial Computations
**Rule:** Do not use `useMemo` for simple calculations like counts or string concatenations; reserve memoization for expensive computations or objects that would trigger unnecessary re-renders.

**Category:** performance

### 70. Distinguish None Vs Empty Semantics
**Rule:** When an optional collection field has different semantic meanings for absence (None = unknown/legacy) vs empty (Some(empty) = explicitly none), preserve that distinction rather than collapsing both to None.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.8
**Review count:** 8
**Source PRs:** #47216, #44810, #40730
**Modules:** projects, remote-file-system, aigateway
**Trigger:** You're working with an optional collection field (e.g., Option[Seq[T]], Option[Set[T]]) where None and Some(empty) carry different domain meanings — such as None meaning 'unknown/legacy/not set' versus Some(Seq.empty) meaning 'the user explicitly chose none'.
**Rationale:** Collapsing None and Some(empty) destroys domain information that downstream consumers rely on — for example, a migration backfill needs to know which records are legacy (unknown) versus which were explicitly cleared by a user. This distinction is especially critical at API boundaries where clients make decisions based on absence vs emptiness.

### 88. Use Enums For Related Constant Groups
**Rule:** When defining a set of related string or numeric constants, use an enum (or a const object with an extracted type) rather than loose constants, and tie the type to the enum keys for type safety.

**Category:** naming
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.8
**Review count:** 8
**Source PRs:** #40850, #46486, #41575, #40438, #45284, #45235
**Modules:** frontend, registered-models, compute-providers, model-serving, secretstore
**Trigger:** You're defining two or more related string or numeric constants that represent a closed set of values (e.g., status codes, permission levels, provider types). You notice them scattered as standalone `const` declarations or inline string literals.
**Rationale:** Loose constants let invalid values slip through at compile time and make it easy to forget a case when the set grows. Enums (or const objects with derived types) create a single source of truth that the type checker enforces at every usage site, catching typos and missing branches before they reach production.

### 89. Use Styled Components, Theme Tokens, And Named Constants Instead Of Inline Styles

### 90. Validate Shared Component Changes For Regressions
**Rule:** When modifying shared/base components (e.g., CodeEditor), manually validate that changes do not introduce regressions in existing consumers, especially for interactive behaviors like auto-close brackets.

**Category:** testing
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.8
**Review count:** 8
**Source PRs:** #44231, #42276, #42514, #42499, #45109, #40076, #46586
**Modules:** frontend, remote-file-system
**Trigger:** You're modifying a shared or base component (e.g., CodeEditor, Modal, DataTable) that is consumed by multiple features or modules. You need to ensure your changes don't break interactive behaviors, styling, or props contracts in existing consumers.
**Rationale:** Shared components are high-leverage code — a single change propagates to every consumer, so a fix in one context can silently break interactive behaviors in others. Manual validation is essential because automated tests rarely cover the full matrix of interactive behaviors (keyboard shortcuts, focus management, auto-complete) across all consuming contexts.

### 108. Use Existing Components Before Overriding
**Rule:** Before overriding component styles, check if the design system component has been updated to support the desired appearance natively; validate discrepancies with UX.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.7
**Review count:** 7
**Source PRs:** #44843, #41365, #42693, #42458, #42713
**Modules:** frontend
**Trigger:** You're adding custom CSS overrides or styled-components wrappers to change the appearance of a design system component (e.g., Ant Design Button, Modal, Select). You're tempted to override tokens, class names, or inject inline styles to get the look you want.
**Rationale:** Style overrides on design system components create maintenance debt that silently breaks on library upgrades and causes visual inconsistencies across the product. Validating with UX first catches cases where the design system already supports the desired appearance or where the spec itself should be updated upstream.

### 110. Use Url/Uri Builder Classes Instead Of String Concatenation

### 125. Log Context Not Just Exception Message
**Rule:** When logging exceptions, pass the full exception object as a parameter (which includes the stack trace) and write a descriptive log message about the operation context, rather than just logging ex.getMessage.

**Category:** logging

---

### 126. Make Polling Intervals Configurable Via Central Config
**Rule:** When introducing polling or periodic checks against external services, expose the interval as a configurable parameter (e.g., via Central Config) rather than hardcoding it, enabling tuning without redeployment.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.6
**Review count:** 6
**Source PRs:** #41485, #39994, #45083, #43925, #43686, #44488
**Modules:** projects, server, apps, data-plane, frontend, repoman
**Trigger:** You're introducing a polling loop, periodic health check, or scheduled retry against an external service (e.g., polling execution status, refreshing tokens, checking data-plane readiness). You're about to hardcode a duration literal like `5.seconds` or `30000` directly in the polling logic.
**Rationale:** Hardcoded polling intervals force a full build-and-deploy cycle to tune timing, which is especially costly during incidents when you need to back off an overwhelmed service immediately. Exposing intervals via Central Config lets operators adjust polling frequency in production without redeployment, enabling rapid response to load spikes and per-environment tuning.

### 142. Add Tests For New Behavior Paths

---

### 143. Always Provide Error Feedback For Api Dependent Rendering
**Rule:** When a component conditionally renders based on an API response, always handle and surface errors to the user (e.g., via a toast notification) — otherwise a failed request results in a blank screen with no explanation.

**Category:** error-handling
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #44194, #44159, #41878, #40461, #42172
**Modules:** frontend
**Trigger:** You're writing a component that conditionally renders content based on data fetched from an API, such as showing a list only after a successful response or toggling UI based on a feature flag endpoint.
**Rationale:** When an API call fails silently and the component returns null or an empty fragment, users see a blank screen with no indication of what went wrong or how to recover. Surfacing errors via toast notifications and fallback UI preserves user confidence and makes failures diagnosable.

---

### 144. Api Docs Should Not Reference Implementation Details
**Rule:** API documentation should describe behavior abstractly rather than referencing current implementation details (such as specific upsert keys or internal identifiers) that may change as the system evolves.

**Category:** api-design
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #47200, #46860
**Modules:** nucleus, gen-ai

---

### 145. Api Response Must Match Schema Contract
**Rule:** When an API schema marks fields as required, do not silently map missing values to empty strings or defaults; either ensure the values are present or make the schema reflect the actual optionality.

**Category:** api-design
**Mode:** hook
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #47212
**Modules:** apps
**Trigger:** You're defining or modifying an API endpoint whose response schema marks certain fields as required, and the underlying data source may not always provide values for those fields.
**Rationale:** When an API contract says a field is required but the implementation silently substitutes empty strings or defaults, consumers trust the contract and skip null checks—leading to subtle bugs, broken UI displays, and data integrity issues that are hard to trace back to the source.

---

### 146. Audit All Usages When Fixing A Utility Misuse
**Rule:** When a reviewer identifies a misuse of a utility function, systematically review all call sites for the same mistake rather than fixing only the commented instance.

**Category:** code-organization
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #42141, #39449, #47262, #46336
**Modules:** frontend, server, apps, registered-models
**Trigger:** You're fixing a misuse of a utility function or helper method that a reviewer flagged in a PR. Before submitting your fix, you need to check whether the same misuse exists elsewhere in the codebase.
**Rationale:** Fixing only the flagged instance leaves identical bugs lurking elsewhere, which often surface as production incidents weeks later. A systematic audit turns a single code review comment into a codebase-wide quality improvement and prevents the same review feedback from recurring across future PRs.

---

### 147. Audit Events Must Include Human Readable Names

**Category:** logging

**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5

**Modules:** extensions

---

### 148. Avoid Loose Object Type

### 149. Avoid Over Abstraction For Simple Needs
**Rule:** Do not force-fit a complex abstraction (like a generic data-fetching hook) when the resulting workarounds outweigh the benefits; prefer simpler, direct implementations when the abstraction adds more complexity than value.

**Category:** architecture

**Modules:** frontend, executor, server

---

### 150. Avoid Redundant React State
**Rule:** Do not duplicate the same data across multiple React state variables; if a single state object (e.g., editedLauncher) already tracks the full form state, derive values from it rather than maintaining separate parallel state.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #45573, #45719, #44942, #44544, #44563
**Modules:** frontend

---

### 151. Await Async Functions In Try Catch Blocks
**Rule:** When calling an async function inside a try-catch block, you must `await` the call; otherwise the catch block will not intercept errors from the async operation.

**Category:** error-handling
**Mode:** hook
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #42586, #43908, #40830
**Modules:** frontend
**Trigger:** You're calling an async function inside a try-catch block and need errors from that operation to be caught and handled locally.
**Rationale:** Without `await`, the async call returns a pending promise and execution immediately continues to the success path. The promise rejects later outside the try-catch scope, producing an unhandled rejection instead of triggering the catch block.

---

### 152. Boolean Prop Shorthand
**Rule:** When passing a boolean prop with value true in JSX, use the shorthand form (e.g., `<Route exact>` instead of `<Route exact={true}>`).

**Category:** naming
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #41231, #42177, #42272, #42627
**Modules:** frontend

---

### 153. Cache Infrequently Changing Data Instead Of Fetching On Every Request
**Rule:** When upstream data changes rarely (e.g., once every few months), avoid performing heavy IO on every endpoint call; use caching or a check-before-fetch strategy to reduce database load.

**Category:** performance
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #40900, #42095
**Modules:** projects, model-serving
**Trigger:** You're writing an endpoint or service method that fetches data from the database or an external service on every call, but the underlying data changes rarely (e.g., project settings, model metadata, feature flags that update once every few weeks or months).
**Rationale:** When data changes infrequently but is read on every request, repeated database or service calls add unnecessary latency and load. Caching with proper invalidation eliminates redundant IO, reduces p99 latency, and protects downstream datastores during traffic spikes.

---

### 154. Centralize Shared Constants In Utility Modules
**Rule:** Do not hardcode shared values (URLs, support links, config strings) in feature components; place them in the appropriate shared utility module (e.g., supportUtil.ts) so they can be maintained in one place.

**Category:** code-organization
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5

### 169. Explicit Restriction Over Silent Failure

### 170. Fail Closed Default For Permissions
**Rule:** Default boolean values for permission or limit checks should fail closed (restrict access) rather than fail open (allow access), so that errors don't silently grant unauthorized operations.

**Category:** security
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.5

**Source PRs:** #45518, #47131, #41878
**Modules:** frontend, dataset-rw

---

### 171. Fail Loudly On Impossible Cases Instead Of Silently Skipping
**Rule:** When a code path is believed to be impossible, throw an exception rather than silently skipping or returning a default value, so violations of assumptions surface immediately.

**Category:** error-handling
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #47216
**Modules:** apps

---

### 172. Handle Async Errors And Show Loading Feedback
**Rule:** When calling an async API in a React component, catch errors gracefully and show a loading indicator (spinner or disabled state) while the request is in flight.

**Category:** error-handling
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #41411, #43610, #41183
**Modules:** frontend
**Trigger:** You're writing a React component that calls an async API (e.g., fetch, axios, or a service client) and renders the result. You need to handle the loading and error states so users aren't left staring at a blank screen or silently losing data.
**Rationale:** Without loading indicators, users can't tell if the app is working or broken, leading to duplicate clicks and confusion. Silently swallowed errors leave users at a dead end with no way to recover, which directly violates Domino's UX principles of increasing user confidence and paving a smooth path.

---

### 173. Guard Expensive Calls With Early Return
**Rule:** Move feature flag checks and expensive service calls inside the branch that actually needs them, so they are skipped when the result would be unused (e.g., when a list is empty).

**Category:** performance
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5

**Modules:** apps

### 174. Handle Archived Entities In Indexing
**Rule:** Search and index operations must handle archived or deleted entities gracefully (e.g., by removing stale index entries) and should include tests covering those states.

### 175. Isolate Loop Iterations To Fail Gracefully
**Rule:** When iterating over items that require remediation or processing, extract the loop body into its own function with independent error handling so a failure on one item does not prevent processing the rest.

### 182. Prefer Library Constructs Over Manual Parsing

### 183. Preserve Existing Validation When Refactoring Code Paths
**Rule:** When creating new code paths that replace or parallel existing ones, audit the original path for validation steps (guardrails, permission checks) and ensure they are carried over.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #47189, #44488, #43785
**Modules:** apps, projects, frontend
**Trigger:** You're creating a new code path that replaces, wraps, or runs parallel to an existing one — such as extracting a service method, adding a new API endpoint that duplicates existing functionality, or refactoring a controller action into a different execution flow.
**Rationale:** Dropped validations in parallel code paths create security gaps and silent regressions that are hard to detect — users can bypass permission checks or guardrails simply by hitting the newer endpoint. These bugs often reach production because the new path appears to work correctly in the happy path.

---

### 184. Remove Unnecessary React Fragments

### 189. Unit Tests For New Logic
**Rule:** Add unit tests for newly introduced or modified logic paths, especially when handling new data variants or edge cases.

**Category:** testing
**Mode:** ambient

**Modules:** repoman, registered-models, server, compute-grid

---

### 190. Stream Large Collections Instead Of Loading All
**Rule:** When processing all entities (e.g., for indexing or batch operations), use lazy/streaming collections instead of loading everything into memory at once to avoid OOM issues at scale.

**Category:** performance
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #47170
**Modules:** server
**Trigger:** You're writing a batch operation, indexing job, or migration that processes all entities of a given type. You're about to call a method that returns a full List or Seq of all records from the database.
**Rationale:** Loading all entities into memory at once creates a ticking OOM bomb — it works in dev and staging but fails catastrophically when production data grows past heap capacity. Streaming with backpressure keeps memory usage constant regardless of dataset size, making batch operations safe at any scale.

---

### 191. Test Degraded Failure Paths
**Rule:** When a dependency can throw and is caught with NonFatal, write a test verifying the caller degrades gracefully (e.g., returns a default or partial result) rather than propagating the failure.

**Category:** testing
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #47212
**Modules:** apps

---

### 192. Test Negative Cases Explicitly
**Rule:** Tests should explicitly assert that excluded or filtered-out items are absent from results, not just verify the count and contents of included items.

**Category:** testing
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #46790, #47308, #44921
**Modules:** registered-models, server

---

### 193. Unit Test Feature Flag Code Paths
**Rule:** When adding behavior gated by a feature flag, add unit tests that validate the code path under the new flag to prevent regressions from untested branches.

**Category:** testing
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #40663, #39933, #44406
**Modules:** server, frontend

---

### 194. Use Atomic Field Updates For Concurrent Safety
**Rule:** When updating a single field on a database record, update only that field directly rather than reading the entire object into memory, modifying it, and saving it back, to avoid overwriting concurrent updates to other fields.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #46392, #47169
**Modules:** projects, extensions
**Trigger:** You're writing code that updates a single field on a database record, and you're tempted to fetch the entire object, modify the field in memory, and save the whole object back.
**Rationale:** Read-modify-write cycles create a race condition window where concurrent updates to other fields on the same record are silently lost. Atomic field-level updates eliminate this window entirely and also reduce the payload sent to the database.

---

### 195. Use Correct Color Token Category
**Rule:** Use color tokens from the correct semantic category — text color tokens for text, background tokens for backgrounds, border tokens for borders — even if the hex values happen to match.

**Category:** naming
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #45899, #46578, #45869, #44795, #44644
**Modules:** frontend, server

### 196. Use Correct Http Status Codes For Api Responses

**Confidence:** 0.5

### 197. Use Correct Http Verbs For Api Semantics

**Category:** api-design

### 204. Use Project Test Utilities For Dom Queries

### 205. Use Semantic Html Elements For Interactive Controls

### 206. Validate Assumptions About Required Fields
**Rule:** When accessing a field assumed to always be present (e.g., via .get), verify and document that the field is guaranteed to exist; otherwise handle the missing case to avoid runtime exceptions.

**Category:** error-handling
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #47265, #47308
**Modules:** apps, server

---

### 207. Validate Database Query Scalability With Dynamic Filter Lists
**Rule:** When passing a dynamically-sized list of IDs to a database query (e.g., Mongo $in), verify that the list is bounded, the target field is indexed, and the query document stays within size limits.

**Category:** performance
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #47233
**Modules:** apps
**Trigger:** You're writing a database query that passes a dynamically-sized collection of IDs into a filter operator like Mongo's $in, where the list size depends on runtime data such as user selections, project membership, or batch job inputs.
**Rationale:** An unbounded $in list can cause full collection scans if the target field is unindexed, blow past MongoDB's 16 MB document size limit, and degrade database performance for all tenants. Bounding and chunking the list ensures predictable query cost and prevents cascading slowdowns in multi-tenant environments.

---

### 208. Verify Backward Compatibility On Field Optionality Change
**Rule:** When changing a DTO field from required to optional, verify backward compatibility with existing consumers by running end-to-end tests before merging.

**Category:** api-design
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #47202, #47189
**Modules:** projects, apps

---

### 209. Verify Shared Component Usage Before Removal
**Rule:** Before removing or renaming props on shared/core UI components, verify that no other consumers depend on them, especially when the change won't merge soon.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.5
**Review count:** 5
**Source PRs:** #42070, #40370, #44127, #46041
**Modules:** frontend, apps
**Trigger:** You're modifying, removing, or renaming props on a shared or core UI component (e.g., a design system component, a common layout wrapper, or a reusable form element) that is consumed across multiple modules or teams.
**Rationale:** Shared components often have consumers spread across multiple teams and modules that aren't visible from a single feature branch. Removing props without a full consumer audit and deprecation period causes silent breakage in other teams' code, especially when the change sits unmerged and diverges from trunk.

---

### 217. Api Design Consistency
**Rule:** API documentation and payloads should be semantically accurate, future-proof, and include human-readable fields. Avoid implementation-specific details in docs, ensure required fields are never silently empty, and use consistent PATCH semantics.

**Category:** api-design

**Modules:** nucleus, apps, extensions, global
**Trigger:** When writing or modifying API schemas, documentation, PATCH endpoints, or audit event payloads
**Rationale:** Implementation-specific docs break when internals change. Silently empty required fields confuse API consumers. Missing human-readable names force users to do extra lookups. Reviewers consistently flag these across nucleus, apps, and extensions.

### 219. Assert Against Known Values Not Derived Proxies

### 220. Avoid Inline Styles In React Components

### 221. Avoid Nested Css Selectors In Styled Components

### 222. Avoid Redundant Database Calls For Consistency
**Rule:** When the same data is needed at multiple layers (e.g., controller and service), fetch it once and pass it as a parameter rather than making redundant database calls, both for performance and to avoid inconsistency if the data changes between calls.

**Category:** performance

### 223. Avoid Unnecessary Container Components
**Rule:** Do not create a container/wrapper component when there is no significant business logic or backend calls to justify the separation from the presentational component.

**Category:** architecture

**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #40687, #44842
**Modules:** frontend

---

### 224. Avoid Unsafe Zero Defaults For Config Driven Limits
**Rule:** When a configuration value controls a limit (e.g., max file size), do not default to 0 if undefined — a zero default can silently block all operations unless explicitly handled as a special case.

**Category:** error-handling
**Mode:** hook
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #44194, #47271
**Modules:** frontend, personalaccesstoken
**Trigger:** You're reading a configuration value that controls a limit (e.g., max file size, max token count, rate limit threshold) and providing a fallback default. You're tempted to default to 0 when the config key is missing or undefined.
**Rationale:** A zero default for a config-driven limit silently blocks all operations that check against it (since every positive value exceeds 0), causing hard-to-diagnose production outages. Choosing a safe non-zero default ensures the system degrades gracefully when configuration is missing rather than failing closed without explanation.

---

### 225. Bdd Scenarios Must Have Assertion Steps

### 226. Catch Blocks Need User Feedback

### 230. Consider Downstream Consumer Impact When Fixing Api Bugs
**Rule:** Before fixing a long-standing API bug, assess whether any consumers may have built workarounds that depend on the buggy behavior, and plan for a safe migration path.

**Category:** api-design
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #47232
**Modules:** environments
**Trigger:** You're fixing a long-standing bug in an API response shape, status code, or default value that consumers may have been relying on for months or years. You're about to correct behavior that, while technically wrong, has become the de facto contract.
**Rationale:** Long-standing API bugs become implicit contracts — consumers build workarounds, parsers, and conditional logic around the buggy behavior. Fixing the bug without a migration path silently breaks those consumers, turning a correctness improvement into a production incident.

---

### 231. Consistent Dto Structure For Frontend
**Rule:** Keep API response DTO structures consistent across similar endpoints, even if slightly verbose, so frontend consumers can reuse TypeScript model definitions.

**Category:** api-design
**Mode:** ambient

**Review count:** 4

**Modules:** projects

---

### 232. Consistent Parameter Passing Style
**Rule:** When a function accepts parameters that serve the same role (e.g., all are query params), pass them consistently through the same mechanism (params object vs positional args) rather than mixing styles based on whether they are required or optional.

**Category:** api-design
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4

**Modules:** frontend, compute-providers, server

### 233. Consistent Retry Configuration
**Rule:** Keep retry counts and backoff configurations consistent across the codebase; when a standard exists (e.g., 5 retries), new retry policies should match unless there is a documented reason to differ.

**Category:** architecture

**Confidence:** 0.4

### 234. Consistent Style Definition Location
**Rule:** Keep all styled components in a single location per feature — either all in a dedicated styles file or all co-located in the component file, not split across both.

**Category:** code-organization
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #41477, #41288
**Modules:** frontend

---

### 235. Cross Service Api Endpoint Parity
**Rule:** When adding a new API endpoint in one service, evaluate whether a corresponding endpoint needs to be created in related services that expose similar resources to maintain API parity.

**Category:** api-design
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #47239
**Modules:** dataset-rw
**Trigger:** You're adding a new API endpoint to a service (e.g., dataset-rw) that exposes a resource also accessible through related services or API layers. You need to evaluate whether corresponding endpoints should be created in sibling services to maintain consistent API coverage.
**Rationale:** When related services expose the same resources but have inconsistent endpoint coverage, clients resort to calling internal services directly — bypassing authentication, rate limiting, and API versioning. Maintaining parity prevents fragmented API surfaces and ensures all access paths remain governed.

---

### 236. Deduplicate Collection Values Before Batch Operations
**Rule:** When extracting values from a map or collection for use in a batch lookup or query, deduplicate them first to avoid redundant processing, even if each individual operation is inexpensive.

**Category:** performance
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #47232
**Modules:** environments

---

### 237. Default To Least Privilege On Unknown State
**Rule:** When a user's permission or role state is unknown (e.g., request pending or failed), default to the most restrictive access level rather than granting elevated privileges.

**Category:** security
**Mode:** ambient

### 239. Distinguish Service Failures From Empty Results In Logging

### 244. Document Purpose Of Multiple Implementations

---

### 245. Document Surprising None Semantics
**Rule:** When an optional API field being absent causes destructive behavior (e.g., removing an existing value), document this explicitly in the API and add unit tests, because callers may assume absent fields are simply skipped.

**Category:** api-design
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #40969, #46644
**Modules:** projects, gen-ai
**Trigger:** You're designing or modifying an API endpoint where an optional field's absence (None/null) triggers a destructive or state-changing side effect, such as clearing an existing value, removing a configuration, or resetting to defaults.
**Rationale:** Callers universally assume that omitting an optional field in a partial update means 'leave it unchanged.' When absence instead triggers deletion or clearing, it creates silent data loss bugs that are extremely difficult to diagnose, as the caller's payload looks correct and no error is raised.

---

### 246. Extend Existing Methods Instead Of Creating Parallel Ones
**Rule:** When adding new parameters to a service method, extend the existing method with default-valued parameters instead of creating a new method alongside it, to avoid API clutter and confusion for future developers.

**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #46274, #41063, #41287
**Modules:** apps, server, dataset-rw

### 250. Encode Non Optionality In Types With Runtime Validation
**Rule:** When fields are required for an operation but optional in the data model, declare them as non-optional in the operation's interface and validate their presence at the boundary, throwing if required fields are missing.

**Category:** api-design
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #47189
**Modules:** apps
**Trigger:** You're writing an operation that requires certain fields which are declared as optional (e.g., Option[T]) in the underlying data model or DTO. You need to ensure those fields are present before proceeding with the operation.
**Rationale:** Encoding required fields as non-optional in the operation's interface shifts validation to a single boundary point and lets the compiler enforce correctness downstream, eliminating scattered defensive checks and silent defaults that mask missing data bugs.

### 261. Guard Endpoints With Feature Flags
**Rule:** When adding a feature flag or central config value, also guard the corresponding API endpoints in the same PR rather than leaving them unprotected; the exception thrown should indicate that the feature could be enabled but is not currently active.

**Category:** api-design
**Mode:** hook
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #39933, #42133, #44730, #45002
**Modules:** server, frontend, apps
**Trigger:** You're adding a new feature flag or central configuration value that controls access to a feature. You need to ensure the corresponding API endpoints are also guarded in the same PR.
**Rationale:** Unguarded endpoints expose partially-built features to users before they are ready, creating confusing UX and potential security risks. Guarding endpoints in the same PR as the flag ensures atomic feature gating — the feature is either fully accessible or fully blocked, with no window where endpoints leak through.

### 269. Never Define Components Inside Render Functions

### 271. Place Helpers In Companion Objects
**Rule:** In Scala, place utility functions that are specific to a class in its companion object rather than leaving them as loose functions or mixing them into unrelated classes.

**Category:** code-organization

**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4

**Modules:** repoman, model-serving, data-plane

---

### 272. Parallelize Independent Async Operations
**Rule:** When multiple async operations are independent of each other, execute them in parallel rather than awaiting them sequentially to reduce latency.

**Category:** performance
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #40784, #41832
**Modules:** projects, frontend
**Trigger:** You're writing code that awaits multiple async operations sequentially (e.g., API calls, database queries) where none of the results depend on each other.
**Rationale:** Sequential awaits on independent operations make total latency the sum of all call durations, while parallel execution reduces it to the duration of the slowest call. In frontend code this directly impacts perceived page load time and time-to-interactive.

---

### 276. Place Methods In The Correct Domain Service

### 277. Prefer Case Class Over Tuple

---

### 278. Prefer Concrete Type Injection Over @Named Annotations
**Rule:** When a class needs specific implementations injected, prefer injecting the concrete types directly rather than using @Named annotations on the interface, reserving the interface binding for the facade that other consumers should use.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #47131
**Modules:** dataset-rw
**Trigger:** You're wiring up dependency injection for a class that needs a specific implementation of an interface, and you're considering using @Named annotations to disambiguate between multiple bindings of the same interface.
**Rationale:** @Named annotations introduce fragile string-based coupling that the compiler cannot verify, making typos and refactors silently dangerous. Injecting concrete types directly is type-safe, self-documenting, and keeps the interface binding clean for consumers that genuinely depend on the abstraction.

---

### 291. Reset Ui State On Error Paths
**Rule:** When fetching data that sets multiple state variables, ensure error handlers also reset dependent state (e.g., flags and content) to prevent stale values from a previous successful fetch from persisting.

**Category:** error-handling
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #40716, #44194
**Modules:** frontend
**Trigger:** You're writing a data-fetching function or useEffect that sets multiple pieces of state on success (e.g., a loading flag, content data, metadata). You need to ensure the error/catch path resets all of those same state variables so stale values from a previous successful fetch don't linger in the UI.
**Rationale:** When an error handler only sets an error message without clearing dependent state, the UI can display contradictory information — an error banner alongside stale data from a previous successful request. This misleads users into acting on outdated data and makes error states harder to reason about.

### 301. Strict Equality Operator

### 302. Test All Code Paths
**Rule:** Add tests for all significant code paths and features, not just the primary one; if a module handles multiple cases (e.g., both 'target' and 'location'), each should have dedicated test coverage.

**Confidence:** 0.4

**Modules:** server, dataset-rw

---

### 303. Test At The Appropriate Abstraction Level
**Rule:** When a behavior depends on integration between multiple systems (e.g., browser requests through middleware), acknowledge unit test limitations and ensure an integration or e2e test ticket exists rather than forcing the assertion into the wrong test layer.

**Category:** testing
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #47224
**Modules:** server
**Trigger:** You're writing a test for behavior that spans multiple systems—such as a browser request flowing through authentication middleware, CSRF protection, and into a controller—and you're tempted to assert on the end-to-end outcome within a unit test.
**Rationale:** Forcing integration-level assertions into unit tests leads to brittle mocks that mirror implementation details rather than verifying real behavior, creating a false sense of coverage while the actual cross-system interaction remains untested. Acknowledging the right test layer ensures real bugs are caught where they occur and keeps unit tests fast and maintainable.

---

### 304. Test Class Names Should Match The Implementation They Validate
**Rule:** Name test classes to clearly indicate which specific implementation they are testing, so the purpose remains unambiguous when implementations change.

**Category:** testing
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #47131
**Modules:** dataset-rw

---

### 305. Test Mutations By Asserting State Changes
**Rule:** Update tests should modify a value, then assert that only the targeted field changed and all other fields remain unchanged.

**Category:** testing
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #47169
**Modules:** extensions

### 306. Trace Logging In Client Methods
**Rule:** Add trace-level logging to all client/integration methods, including the method name and all parameters, to aid debugging of cross-service calls.

### 307. Use Named Types Over Tuples For Return Values
**Rule:** When a function returns multiple related values, define a named type or case class instead of returning a tuple, because positional access (e.g., `._1`) harms readability.

### 314. Use Optional Chaining With Nullish Coalescing For Defensive Access

### 317. Validate External Command Output
**Rule:** When invoking external tools like sed or shell commands, run them in a separate step, validate the result is meaningful, and handle exceptions with clear error messages.

**Category:** error-handling
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #47168
**Modules:** server
**Trigger:** You're invoking an external tool or shell command (e.g., sed, grep, curl, or a subprocess) from application code and using its output to drive subsequent logic.
**Rationale:** External commands can fail silently, return empty or malformed output, or hang indefinitely. Validating their results in a separate step prevents corrupt data from propagating through the system and gives operators actionable diagnostics instead of mysterious downstream failures.

---

### 318. Verify Behavioral Compatibility During Migrations
**Rule:** When migrating between SDK versions, verify that serialized representations (toString, JSON, etc.) remain compatible, especially if downstream consumers depend on the format.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #41126, #41159, #46268
**Modules:** common-core, frontend, server
**Trigger:** You're migrating between SDK versions, library upgrades, or replacing an internal dependency, and the old code produced serialized output (toString, JSON, XML, protobuf) that downstream consumers parse or store.
**Rationale:** Serialized representations are implicit API contracts. When an SDK migration silently changes toString or JSON output, downstream consumers (frontends, log pipelines, stored database values) break in ways that unit tests on business logic won't catch.

---

### 319. Verify Changes Are Applied Consistently Across All Relevant Entity Types
**Rule:** When modifying authorization, configuration, or behavior for one entity type (e.g., templates, projects), verify whether the same changes need to be applied to related entity types (e.g., apps, models) to avoid inconsistent behavior.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #42401, #47315, #40798
**Modules:** server, frontend
**Trigger:** You're modifying authorization logic, configuration handling, or behavioral rules for one entity type (e.g., projects, templates, workspaces) and need to determine whether sibling entity types require the same change.
**Rationale:** Entity types that share authorization, configuration, or behavioral contracts often need changes applied in lockstep. Updating only one entity type creates inconsistent behavior that surfaces as subtle bugs — users gain access in one context but not another, or configuration works for projects but silently fails for apps.

---

### 320. Verify Color Token Semantics
**Rule:** When replacing hardcoded colors with design tokens, verify the token's semantic meaning matches the intended use context (e.g., a background token should actually be used for backgrounds, not text).

**Category:** naming
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4

**Modules:** frontend

### 321. Verify Cross Repo Dependencies Before Removal
**Rule:** Before removing environment variables, scripts, or shared resources, search for usages across all consuming repositories and CI pipelines to avoid breaking downstream dependencies.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.4
**Review count:** 4
**Source PRs:** #40806, #40725
**Modules:** build, .circleci
**Trigger:** You're removing or renaming an environment variable, build script, shared configuration, or any resource that other repositories or CI pipelines might consume. You're cleaning up what appears to be dead code in a shared or cross-repo context.
**Rationale:** Shared resources like environment variables and build scripts often have invisible consumers across repository boundaries. Removing them without a cross-repo audit causes cascading CI failures and broken deployments that are difficult to diagnose because the root cause lives in a different repo's commit history.

---

### 330. Assert Response Content Not Just Status

### 331. Assess Shared Component Impact
**Rule:** Before modifying a shared/common component, assess whether the change will cause behavior changes in all consumers, not just the immediate use case.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #45508, #45162, #43610
**Modules:** frontend
**Trigger:** You're modifying a shared or common component (e.g., a reusable Button, Modal, Table, or utility hook) and your change is motivated by a specific feature or use case rather than a universal improvement.
**Rationale:** Shared components form implicit contracts with every consumer. Changing default behavior to serve one use case silently breaks other consumers, causing visual regressions and behavioral surprises that are hard to trace back to the originating PR.

---

### 332. Audit Api Endpoints For Secret Leakage
**Rule:** When exposing configuration or internal data through API endpoints, review whether sensitive values (secrets, credentials) could leak outside their intended security boundary.

**Category:** security
**Mode:** hook
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #41068
**Modules:** internal-info
**Trigger:** You're building or modifying an API endpoint that returns configuration, environment variables, or internal system state. You're exposing data that may contain secrets, credentials, or tokens embedded alongside non-sensitive values.
**Rationale:** API endpoints that serialize full configuration objects or internal state can inadvertently expose secrets like database passwords, API keys, and cloud credentials to users who should never see them. A single leaked credential can compromise an entire environment, so endpoints must use explicit allowlists rather than relying on obscurity or caller discipline.

---

### 333. Authz Checks Even When Stubbed

### 349. Avoid Unsafe Type Assertions That Mask Nullability
**Rule:** Do not use type assertions (e.g., `as SomeType`) to bypass TypeScript's null/undefined checks — verify the value exists at runtime or use proper type narrowing.

**Modules:** frontend

---

### 350. Await Async Permission Checks
**Rule:** When a function like hasAccessToResource can return a Promise, always await it before using its result in a boolean expression; an unresolved Promise is truthy and will bypass the check.

**Category:** error-handling
**Mode:** hook
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #45191, #44497, #44141
**Modules:** frontend
**Trigger:** You're writing a permission or access check that calls a function like hasAccessToResource, canEdit, or similar authorization helper that may return a Promise<boolean> rather than a plain boolean.
**Rationale:** An unawaited Promise is a non-null object and therefore always truthy in JavaScript, so using it directly in a boolean expression silently bypasses the permission check and grants access to every user. This is a security vulnerability that produces no runtime errors and is easy to miss in code review.

---

### 351. Boolean Variables Should Use Descriptive Verb Prefixes
**Rule:** Name boolean variables and props with verb prefixes like `should`, `is`, `has`, or `can` to clearly communicate their purpose (e.g., `shouldDisableHwPicker` instead of a generic name).

**Category:** naming
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #45006, #42987, #45899
**Modules:** frontend

---

### 352. Bug Fix Requires Regression Test
**Rule:** When fixing a bug, add a unit test that would have caught the bug to prevent regressions.

**Category:** testing
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #44014, #41251
**Modules:** server, projects

---

### 353. Cache Repeated Lookups In Event Processing Pipelines
**Rule:** When processing a stream of events that each trigger a database or service lookup, introduce a low-complexity cache to avoid redundant lookups that scale linearly with event volume.

**Category:** performance
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #40839
**Modules:** server
**Trigger:** You're writing an event processing pipeline where each event triggers a database or service lookup (e.g., fetching user details, project metadata, or permission checks), and many events share the same lookup keys.
**Rationale:** Without caching, lookup cost scales linearly with event count rather than with the number of distinct keys, causing unnecessary database load and latency spikes during high-volume event bursts. A simple batch-scoped cache can reduce redundant lookups by 80-90% in typical Domino workloads where many events reference the same project or user.

---

### 354. Case Insensitive String Comparison
**Rule:** Use case-insensitive comparison (e.g., `.toLowerCase()`) when matching user-facing strings like labels, names, or identifiers that may vary in casing.

**Category:** error-handling

**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3

### 356. Clean Up Entire Dependency Chain When Removing Functionality
**Rule:** When removing a feature or module, trace and remove all references including config bindings, injection modules, and test fixtures — don't leave hollowed-out shells.

**Category:** code-organization
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #46950, #45462, #43030
**Modules:** server, frontend
**Trigger:** You're removing a feature, module, or service class and need to ensure no orphaned references remain. You're deleting or deprecating functionality that was wired into dependency injection, configuration, routes, or test fixtures.
**Rationale:** Leftover bindings, config keys, and test fixtures create compile errors, confuse future developers about whether functionality still exists, and accumulate as dead code that obscures the actual system architecture. A clean removal ensures the codebase accurately reflects what the system does.

### 367. Consider Race Conditions In Module Injection
**Rule:** When injecting helpers or dependencies via dynamic module loading, evaluate whether race conditions can occur between modules loading and the helpers becoming available.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #39589
**Modules:** server
**Trigger:** You're injecting helpers, utilities, or dependencies into modules via dynamic module loading (e.g., Guice, MacWire, or custom injection frameworks) where the availability of the injected dependency depends on module initialization order.
**Rationale:** When module initialization order is not explicitly enforced, a consumer can be invoked before its dynamically injected dependency is available, leading to NullPointerExceptions or silently missing behavior in production — failures that are timing-dependent and difficult to reproduce in tests.

### 372. Consistent Search Query Parameter Naming
**Rule:** Use `q` as the query parameter name for search/filter endpoints across all APIs to maintain consistency, and use a more descriptive name like `searchQuery` only internally.

**Category:** api-design
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #40900
**Modules:** projects

### 377. Copy All Attributes When Cloning
**Rule:** When implementing object copy, fork, or clone operations, ensure all relevant attributes are transferred -- review the source model field-by-field to avoid missing properties.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #40784
**Modules:** projects
**Trigger:** You're implementing a copy, fork, or clone operation for a domain object (e.g., forking a project, duplicating a configuration). You need to ensure the new object faithfully reproduces all relevant properties from the source.
**Rationale:** Manually constructing a new object instead of copying from the source leads to silent data loss -- users fork a project expecting an exact replica but discover missing tags, configurations, or settings. Using `copy()` with targeted overrides ensures new fields are inherited by default and forces developers to explicitly decide which fields need special handling.

### 381. Do Not Persist Computed Values In The Database
**Rule:** Fields whose values are derived from other data (e.g., a path computed from a container config) should not be stored in the database; compute them at read time to avoid staleness and maintenance burden.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3

**Modules:** dataset-rw, projects

---

### 382. Delay Render Until Async Deps Loaded
**Rule:** When a component depends on asynchronously loaded data (e.g., locale configuration), consider delaying the render until the data is available to avoid rendering in an incomplete or incorrect state.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #40863
**Modules:** frontend
**Trigger:** You're building a component that depends on asynchronously loaded data—such as locale configuration, feature flags, or user preferences—that must be available before the component can render correctly.
**Rationale:** Rendering before async dependencies are available causes flashes of incorrect content, layout shifts, and subtle bugs where components initialize with stale or default values that don't update cleanly when the real data arrives.

---

### 383. Delete Records Only After Dependent Operations Succeed
**Rule:** When deleting a resource that has dependent external resources (e.g., Kubernetes objects), delete the database record only after the external cleanup succeeds so the record is preserved for retry if cleanup fails.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #40765
**Modules:** model-serving
**Trigger:** You're writing code that deletes a database record for a resource that also has external dependencies (e.g., Kubernetes deployments, services, or ingress objects) that must be cleaned up as part of the deletion workflow.
**Rationale:** If the database record is deleted before external resources are cleaned up and the external cleanup fails, the system loses the reference data needed to locate and retry the cleanup — resulting in orphaned resources that leak infrastructure and require manual intervention to resolve.

---

### 398. Exception Wrappers Must Preserve Cause Chain
**Rule:** When wrapping exceptions across SDK versions, define proper custom exceptions that set message and cause on the parent Throwable; never throw wrapper objects that lose the original stack trace.

**Category:** error-handling
**Mode:** hook
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #41111, #40765
**Modules:** common-core, model-serving
**Trigger:** You're wrapping or re-throwing exceptions across SDK version boundaries or abstraction layers, especially in custom exception classes that translate between internal and external error types.
**Rationale:** Losing the original cause chain makes production debugging extremely difficult because stack traces end at the wrapper instead of showing where the real failure occurred. Preserving the full exception chain ensures that logs, monitoring tools, and developers can trace errors back to their root cause across SDK and abstraction boundaries.

### 400. Extract Api Logic Into Custom Hooks To Reduce Component Complexity
**Rule:** When a React component makes multiple API calls that control rendering, extract the data-fetching and state logic into a custom hook to keep the component focused on presentation and simplify testing.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #44194, #41621
**Modules:** frontend
**Trigger:** You're writing or reviewing a React component that makes multiple API calls (e.g., useQuery, useSWR, fetch) whose loading/error states control conditional rendering. The component mixes data-fetching orchestration with presentation logic, making it hard to test or reason about.
**Rationale:** Mixing multiple API calls into a component forces tests to mock every endpoint and makes the component hard to read as it grows. Extracting a custom hook separates data orchestration from presentation, letting each be tested and modified independently.

### 404. Documentation Discipline
**Rule:** TODOs must reference tracked tickets. Forward-looking assumptions must be documented inline. Interface-layer docs must not reference implementation details from other modules.

**Category:** documentation
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #47178, #47189, #47216
**Modules:** server, apps
**Trigger:** When adding TODO comments, writing docstrings on interface-layer classes, or making assumptions about current system behavior that may change
**Rationale:** Untracked TODOs are never resolved. Undocumented assumptions become invisible tech debt. Cross-module implementation details in interface docs create coupling and break when internals change.

### 405. Domain Logic In Domain Layer

### 406. Early Return Over Deep Nesting
**Rule:** Use early return (guard clause) patterns to exit functions early when preconditions are not met, instead of wrapping the entire function body in a conditional block.

**Category:** code-organization
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #40617, #43344, #42691
**Modules:** system-tests, frontend

---

### 407. Eliminate N Plus One Queries
**Rule:** When a method executes one query per item in a list (N+1 pattern), replace it with a batch query or join to avoid performance degradation as the list grows.

**Category:** performance
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #47189
**Modules:** apps
**Trigger:** You're writing code that iterates over a collection and makes a separate database query or API call for each item, such as fetching details for each project in a list or resolving references one at a time inside a loop.
**Rationale:** N+1 queries scale linearly with collection size, turning a single page load into hundreds of database round-trips under real workloads. Batching collapses N+1 calls into 1 (or a small constant), keeping response times stable as data grows.

---

### 408. Encapsulate Distinct Concerns Into Components

### 417. Fail Explicitly

**Modules:** apps
**Trigger:** When handling unexpected types in match/switch expressions, resolving required fields that may be absent, or encountering states that should be impossible
**Rationale:** Silent returns mask bugs and make debugging harder. Three instances across two PRs from different reviewers show this is a strongly-held team convention. Reviewers explicitly asked for throws over silent skips.

### 428. Include Domain Context In Function And Step Names
**Rule:** Function and step names should include the domain or service they interact with (e.g., 'keycloak') to avoid ambiguity, even if it feels redundant — clarity for readers outweighs brevity.

**Modules:** e2e-tests, apps

---

### 429. Handle Concurrent Request Race Conditions
**Rule:** When implementing policies that enforce uniqueness or singleton constraints, account for race conditions where multiple concurrent requests could bypass the check, especially in distributed systems with multiple service instances.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #42007, #46529
**Modules:** server, gen-ai
**Trigger:** You're implementing a policy that enforces a uniqueness or singleton constraint (e.g., only one active workspace per user, only one default model version) and the check-then-act logic spans separate read and write operations.
**Rationale:** In distributed systems with multiple service instances, a read-check-then-write pattern creates a time-of-check-to-time-of-use (TOCTOU) gap where concurrent requests can both pass the validation and violate the invariant. Pushing constraints to the database or using distributed locks eliminates this class of bug entirely.

---

### 430. Handle Fatal Vs Nonfatal Errors
**Rule:** When using try-catch-finally patterns, ensure that fatal errors are handled distinctly from non-fatal errors so that finally blocks do not execute unintended logic after catastrophic failures.

**Category:** error-handling
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #40765
**Modules:** model-serving
**Trigger:** You're writing try-catch-finally blocks in model serving code where the finally block performs cleanup or state transitions. You need to ensure catastrophic failures (e.g., OutOfMemoryError, fatal connection losses) don't silently execute finally logic that assumes a recoverable state.
**Rationale:** When finally blocks contain state transitions or business logic, catastrophic failures (OOM, stack overflow) can leave the system in an inconsistent state — for example, marking a model as 'ready' when the serving infrastructure is actually corrupted. Separating fatal from non-fatal handling ensures that only truly recoverable errors trigger recovery logic, while fatal errors propagate to supervisory layers that can restart or alert.

---

### 431. Handle Loading And Error States For Async Data Guarding Destructive Actions
**Rule:** When async data is used to guard destructive actions (e.g., allowing deletion), handle loading and error states explicitly — a falsy default during fetch or on failure can incorrectly enable the action.

**Category:** error-handling
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #42954, #41878
**Modules:** frontend
**Trigger:** You're writing a component where an async data fetch determines whether a destructive action (like delete, stop, or terminate) should be enabled or disabled. The guard value defaults to a falsy state before the fetch completes.
**Rationale:** When async guard data defaults to a falsy value during loading or on fetch failure, destructive actions can be incorrectly enabled in the brief window before data arrives — or permanently if the request fails. Explicitly gating on loading and error states ensures destructive operations are never accessible without confirmed authorization data.

---

### 432. Hide Implementation Details In Wrapper Names
**Rule:** When creating wrapper abstractions over third-party SDKs, use generic names (e.g., listObjects) rather than leaking vendor-specific version details (e.g., listObjectsV2) into public APIs.

**Category:** naming
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #41063
**Modules:** server

---

### 433. Honest Return Types
**Rule:** If a method's return value can never vary (e.g., always returns true), refactor the return type to reflect actual behavior (e.g., Unit/void) rather than suggesting a branching outcome.

**Category:** api-design
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #42075, #47313

### 434. Idiomatic Option Handling

**Category:** code-organization
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3

### 435. Implicit Boolean Props

### 436. Import From Internal Component Library, Not Ant Directly

**Category:** architecture

---

### 437. Imports At Top Of File
**Rule:** Place all imports at the top of the file rather than inline so that all dependencies are visible in one place.

**Category:** code-organization
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #46743, #46606, #46791
**Modules:** apps, run

### 447. Logging Level Correctness
**Rule:** Routine operational messages should use DEBUG, not INFO. Warnings should only fire on genuinely unexpected conditions, and log messages must accurately reflect the condition that triggers them.

**Category:** logging
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #47170, #47216, #47233
**Modules:** server, apps
**Trigger:** When adding or modifying log statements, especially when choosing between INFO/DEBUG/WARN levels or writing log message text
**Rationale:** Overly verbose INFO logs create noise in production. Warnings on legitimate conditions cause alert fatigue. Inaccurate log messages mislead on-call engineers. Reviewers enforce logging discipline across multiple PRs.

---

### 448. Match Specific Error Messages For Retry Logic
**Rule:** When implementing retry logic for opaque exceptions, match on specific known error messages rather than broad exception types to avoid retrying non-retryable failures.

**Category:** error-handling
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #41280, #40443
**Modules:** runprep, system-tests
**Trigger:** You're implementing retry logic around an operation that throws a broad or opaque exception type (e.g., RuntimeException, IOException) where only certain failure modes are actually retryable.
**Rationale:** Broad exception-type matching in retry logic silently swallows non-transient failures, causing delayed error propagation, wasted resources, and misleading timeout errors that mask the real root cause. Matching on specific known error messages ensures only genuinely transient failures are retried while permanent failures surface immediately.

---

### 449. Minimize Io Operations In Data Synchronization Logic
**Rule:** When synchronizing upstream data with a local database, consolidate queries into bulk operations rather than performing per-record IO; consider strategies like remove-all-and-reinsert for simplicity.

**Category:** performance
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #40900
**Modules:** projects
**Trigger:** You're writing data synchronization logic that pulls records from an upstream source and updates a local database to match. You notice the sync iterates over each record individually, issuing separate queries for existence checks, inserts, updates, or deletes.
**Rationale:** Per-record IO in sync loops produces O(n) database round-trips, which degrades linearly with dataset size and can saturate connection pools or cause timeouts under load. Bulk operations reduce this to O(1) or O(n/batchSize) round-trips, making sync performance predictable and keeping database load stable as the upstream dataset grows.

---

### 450. Move Helpers To Utils Files
**Rule:** Extract utility functions and helper logic out of component files into dedicated utils files to keep components focused and helpers reusable.

**Category:** code-organization
**Mode:** ambient
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #40399, #45699, #45423

### 455. Never Disable Eslint Exhaustive Deps Rule In Hooks

### 466. No Success Logic In Finally

### 472. Place Mapping Logic On Domain Class
**Rule:** Place conversion or mapping logic on the domain class or its companion object rather than in an unrelated service, so the logic is co-located with the type it transforms.

**Modules:** server

---

### 473. Plan Data Migrations For New Fields On Existing Records
**Rule:** When adding a new tag, field, or classification to an entity, plan a migration to backfill the value on all existing records, not just newly created ones.

**Category:** architecture
**Mode:** active
**Confidence:** 0.3
**Review count:** 3
**Source PRs:** #46347, #47189
**Modules:** registered-models, apps
**Trigger:** You're adding a new field, tag, or classification to an existing entity (e.g., a new status enum, a visibility flag, or a category label) and writing code that only sets the value on newly created records.
**Rationale:** Existing records won't magically acquire new fields — without a backfill migration, queries that filter or sort on the new field will silently exclude legacy data, and UI components that assume the field is present will break or display incorrect state for older entities.

### 474. Poll Instead Of Sleep In Tests

### 483. Prefer Patch Over Put For Updates

### 487. Preserve Eslint Disable Intent
